Local News Two

The Da Yun Steamer Capsizes in Baozhen, Between Shanghai and Chongming 178

▲ More Than 200 Passengers Rescued

▲ Approximately Eighty People Drowned

The Chongming ferry "Da Yun" belonging to the Da Yun Steamer Company of Shanghai's South City capsized yesterday morning in Baozhen Harbor while en route from Chongming to Shanghai, resulting in the drowning of nearly one hundred passengers. Our reporter specifically visited the company to thoroughly investigate the matter, and the details of the accident are recorded as follows:

▲ Top-Heaviness: The "Da Yun" departed from Chongming at 7:00 AM yesterday morning, carrying 600 bales of cotton at Nanhang Port, destined for the Datong Textile Mill in Baozhen Harbor. The cotton was loaded on the deck, while the cabins inside the ship were empty, carrying only more than 300 passengers. As a result, the ship became top-heavy, with the deck being heavier than the hull. The "Da Yun" was passing through Er Tiao Shu and Xin Kaihe to dock at Baozhen Harbor at 9:20 AM. Just as the ship was dropping anchor, it unexpectedly capsized due to the impact of the tide, resulting in a major tragedy.

▲ Ship Lies on its Side: The "Da Yun" docked at the Baozhen Harbor pier at 9:25 AM. The stern cable had already been secured, and passengers were coming out of the cabins towards the left side of the deck, preparing to disembark. Unexpectedly, at this moment, the tide was surging, causing the ship to lean inward. It was hit by the tide, causing the "Da Yun" to suddenly fall sideways towards the pier and instantly capsize, lying flat on the river surface. Many items from inside the ship fell into the harbor.

▲ Passengers Fall into the Water: When the "Da Yun" capsized, the stern cable did not break. Initially, the ship's smokestack rested on the pier, causing the ship to lie flat on the harbor surface. The total number of passengers on board, including those who disembarked at Nanmen Port (over eighty), Er Tiao Shu (over forty), and Xin Kaihe (over fifty), was approximately three hundred. Among them, some who had already reached the deck also fell into the water when the ship capsized. Except for the crew, sailors, and passengers who jumped onto the pier during the capsizing, at least two hundred seventy or eighty people fell into the water on the spot.

▲ Some Rescued: Those who fell into the water from the deck were mostly close to the pier, making it easier to rescue them. On the spot, local fishermen from the pier rescued over one hundred people. At that time, the "Yong Zhou" ferry, which was also en route to Shanghai, arrived at Baozhen Harbor. Seeing the "Da Yun" capsized, the owner of the "Yong Zhou", Pang Canlin, quickly released sampans to assist in the rescue, rescuing more than twenty passengers who had fallen into the water. A sailboat also rescued more than thirty people. The "Da Yun's" rowing boats also rescued more than thirty people. According to Pang Canlin, who spoke to our reporter, he personally saw the rescue of about two hundred twenty passengers. Finally, the "Yong Zhou" ferry also rescued two passengers, Xu Zhengfu and others, as well as a suitcase from the harbor. The suitcase has been brought to Shanghai, awaiting identification.

▲ Number of Casualties: Many passengers in the "Da Yun" have not been rescued. After the ship capsized, it moved outwards and the hull was submerged in the water, with the smokestack also submerged. Passengers inside the cabins who did not have time to escape were mostly trapped inside the ship. The doors of each cabin were closed, making it impossible to open them. Those trapped inside the ship were certain to have all died. Currently, the company has not provided an exact number, but according to eyewitnesses, it is estimated that the number of crew and passengers who drowned inside the ship and in the water is about seventy or eighty. When the "Yong Zhou" ferry left Shanghai, it still saw victims poking their heads out of the ventilation holes in the ship, crying out for help, but there was no way to get them out. Alas!

▲ Ferries Dispatched for Rescue: Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, the Shanghai Da Yun Company received a telegram reporting the accident, but the message was very brief, only saying that the "Da Yun" carrying 600 bales of cotton capsized in Baozhen. Upon receiving the news, the assistant manager, Du Shaoshi, personally took the company's "Dalian" ferry to Baozhen Harbor for inspection and to discuss rescue methods. According to Mr. Lu of the company, details would be available at 4:00 AM this morning, when Mr. Du returns to Shanghai.

▲ Ship Submerged: The "Yong Zhou" ferry left Baozhen Harbor at approximately 11:00 AM, seeing that the "Da Yun" had already capsized in the harbor. The stern cable was still secured, with the bow facing southeast and the stern facing northwest, about fifty or sixty feet from the pier. The front of the "Da Yun's" hull was still exposed above the water by about three feet, while the stern was submerged and out of sight. The "Da Yun" was built by the Yongyu Company in 1921, with a load capacity of 287 tons, a displacement of 311 tons, a length of 142 feet, a width of 25 feet, and a draft of 7 feet 4 inches. The engine was a two-linked type, with a 400-horsepower engine.

▲ Overview of Losses: This time, the "Da Yun" only had 600 bales of cotton on board, and there were not many goods inside the ship. However, the luggage and belongings of the passengers and crew inside the ship were all lost. Therefore, including the loss of the ship itself, the total loss is estimated at sixty to seventy thousand yuan. The ship was not insured. The shipowner Yang Asan, the chief mate Chen Yunlong, and the second mate Hong Fusheng, are reported to have all escaped and are now in Baozhen Harbor.

Two Chen Tugens 179

▲ The Detention Center Released the Wrong Criminal

▲ The Murderer was Substituted and Released

Ling Jiannan, the owner of a leather shoe store in Ximen Ningkangli, was axed to death by Chen Tugen (formerly a lottery tout), a detective from the reformed Public Security Bureau, Wang Wencai, out of personal revenge. The widow captured the murderer Chen Tugen on the spot and sent him to the District Court for detention. At the same time, the widow also sued Wang Wencai and the old man Huang Zicheng. The case is still under investigation. Unexpectedly, on September 1st, another lottery boatman, also named Chen Tugen, claimed to be an apprentice of the Chen Tugen in the murder case. Originally, he was not surnamed Chen Tugen, but somehow he was deliberately arrested and also sent to the District Court under the same name. After investigation and prosecution, he was sentenced to fifteen days of detention. After deducting the number of days of detention, there were few days left. The court then ordered the detention center to carry out the sentence. The murderer Chen Tugen was detained in cell number 9, while the lottery Chen Tugen was detained in cell number 11. However, due to the detention center's previous mistake in releasing the wrong criminal, all defendants were photographed to avoid errors. Unexpectedly, the two Chen Tugens switched cells. Until five days ago, the lottery Chen Tugen should have been released. Unexpectedly, the murderer Chen Tugen was substituted and released. The officials in the detention center did not check or inquire, resulting in the escape of a serious offender. It has now come to light, but there is no way to find him. However, the widow Ling Ni has learned about this from outside and has hired a lawyer to file a complaint. However, the warden stated that if anyone can capture Chen Tugen, he is willing to offer a large reward.

▲ Using Gambling to Deceive and Obtain Wealth

▲ 10,000 Gold Lost in an Instant

Lu Shichang, the owner of the Yueji Construction Company at No. 51 Putuo Road, also operates a real estate business. Previously, through the introduction of Wang Guangfu and Zhang Xuesheng, he met Zhang Jiayue from Zhejiang for buying and selling land. They interacted with each other and gradually became familiar. After Xu left, Zhang told Lu about Xu's background, saying that Xu had a brother who had recently come to Shanghai and was addicted to gambling and extremely extravagant. Although his wealth was abundant, it would be difficult to maintain it for long. Instead of letting him waste it, they could use some means to obtain it. If they obtained the money, they could donate it to charity, which would be more beneficial than wasting it on empty pleasures. Lu was moved by his words. Zhang, knowing his intention, continued, "I have already arranged a gambling game, but I need a large sum of money. After repeated preparations, I am still short of over 10,000 gold. Please lend me the money temporarily. After the game is over, I will return it and give you a small reward." Lu agreed. On the afternoon of the 11th, Lu brought 10,000 yuan and handed it over to Zhang and Xu for gambling. In a short time, Zhang lost heavily and his funds were exhausted. Zhang comforted Lu, saying, "I will have a large sum of money coming in soon, and I will find a way to return the money I borrowed from you." Lu silently returned home. After thinking about it all night, the next morning he reported it to the Putuo Road Police Station and sent detectives Zhao Rongsen and Wu Changkai to Baek Road to arrest Zhang and Xu Boming and confiscate various items. They were taken to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Special District Court, where Judge Wu Zhen interrogated them. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu presented the case and requested a postponement for investigation. When questioned, the defendants completely denied the charges and hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to defend them, requesting bail. Judge Wu stated that the case still needed investigation and ordered the defendants to be detained and postponed the hearing.

Henan Red Spear Society Bandit Provincial Wang Huiming Released by Public Security Bureau 187

The Henan Provincial Government captured Red Spear Society ringleader Wang Huiming and others around August of this year. According to their confessions, their organization was based in Shanghai. To thoroughly eradicate the evil, the provincial authorities requested the Shanghai Municipal Government's assistance in investigation and arrest. The Municipal Government instructed the Public Security Bureau to dispatch detectives, who, on the 23rd of last month, in conjunction with Chinese and foreign detectives from the Public Concession Police, secretly went to the organization established by the bandit in Huade Road, arrested Wang Shaolin, a member of the society, and sent him to the Second Branch of the High Court for interrogation. Because the Municipal Public Security Bureau applied to transfer the bandit for questioning, they were ordered to present evidence for further review. Yesterday morning, presiding Judge Yu Hua and Assessors Zhao and Guo of the Criminal Division of the Second Branch of the High Court held another hearing. Attorney Zhan Jifeng, the legal advisor of the Public Security Bureau, presented a copy of Wang Huiming's confession, proving that the defendant was indeed an accomplice of the criminals captured in Henan Province. However, when questioned, Wang Shaolin denied being a bandit and claimed not to know Wang Huiming. Subsequently, Attorney Li Zhishan of the police stated that the Municipal Public Security Bureau's attorney had presented substantial evidence, which was credible, and the police agreed to the request for transfer. The defendant's defense attorney then rose to object, arguing that the defendant's crime occurred in the Public Concession and should be under the jurisdiction of the court. The Public Security Bureau's request for transfer was illegal and violated the agreement. Attorney Zhan immediately rebutted, stating that the defendant was a co-conspirator in the bandit organization uncovered by the Henan Provincial Government. According to the law, the official agency that first prosecutes has the jurisdiction to try accomplices, without doubt. To say that it violates the agreement is even more unfounded. The agreement was made between the national government and the consular body, and the Municipal Council represents the interests of the consular body. Now that the Municipal Council's attorney has expressed agreement, it is inappropriate for the national attorney to claim that it violates the agreement. The defense's position is inconsistent. The transfer of the defendant to the Public Security Bureau is in accordance with the agreement and procedures. Judge Yu then adjourned with the assessors for about ten minutes. Upon returning to the bench, he announced that Wang Shaolin should be allowed to be taken by the Public Security Bureau for investigation and handling. Upon hearing the verdict, the defendant's attorney immediately requested a temporary stay of execution in order to file an appeal. After consultation with the presiding judge and assessors, Judge Yu rejected the request in court and ordered Wang Shaolin to be taken away by detectives from the Public Security Bureau.

Three Brothers Rescue Two Orphaned Girls 189

▲ Cai Yousen Has the Face of a Beast

▲ Hongde Church Practices Righteousness and Collects Funds

▲ The Children's Welfare Association Implements Relief

▲ Zhuji County Makes Every Effort to Help

Hongde Church on Doule'an Road in this city was where Pastor Jiang Shixu and Secretary Cai Youzhai of the Christian Church, were martyred during the January 28th Incident of this year. Mr. Cai was from Zhuji. His wife died early, leaving only three daughters: the eldest, Zhizhen, 17 years old; the second, Renzhen, 14 years old; and the youngest, Yongzhen, 12 years old. Father and daughters depended on each other for life. After his sudden and tragic death, the three orphaned girls were cared for by Hongde Church, which practiced righteousness and raised funds to support them. Zhizhen, being older, was sent to the Women and Children's Hospital to learn nursing. Renzhen and Yongzhen, being younger, were sent to Xinde School to study. In July, Cai Youlin, claiming to be Youzhai's younger brother, came to the church to visit his nieces. The church immediately sent someone to guide him to Xinde School and notified the principal to let Renzhen and Yongzhen meet him, confirming that he was their uncle. The next day, Yousen went to the school alone and asked the principal for a week's leave to take the two girls back to their ancestral home in Zhuji to comfort their grandmother, who longed to see her granddaughters. The principal trusted him without doubt and handed the two girls over to Yousen to take back. Unexpectedly, there was no news. It was then discovered that Cai Yousen had used the grandmother's name to deceive the two girls and hide them in Puliwu, near Fengqiao Town in Zhuji, with the intention of selling them. On September 30th, Cai Zhizhen tearfully appealed to the Chinese Children's Welfare Association, requesting relief. The association immediately selected representatives to prepare a document requesting the Zhuji County government to assist in the investigation and punish the crime according to law. County Magistrate Wang immediately sent police to accompany the representatives to Puliwu for investigation. The whereabouts of the two girls were discovered, and a price of 150 yuan each had been agreed upon, and the deal was about to be concluded. The police immediately rescued the two girls, and Cai Yousen escaped upon hearing the news. The representatives could not stay long and sent a letter to the county government requesting that the two orphaned girls be handed over to them to be taken back to their original school in Shanghai to study, and requesting that Cai Yousen be arrested and brought to justice. The county magistrate approved the request. The representatives brought Renzhen and Yongzhen back to Shanghai on Double Tenth Day. The director of Hongde Church requested that the two orphaned girls be sent to the Children's Welfare Association for resettlement. The association, being responsible for children's welfare, immediately sent the two girls to the Children's Welfare Education Institute's Children's Welfare Primary School to study. The two orphans were thus saved from danger. As for Cai Yousen's inhumane actions, it is hoped that County Magistrate Wang will arrest him and punish him according to law, to satisfy the public.

Pimping Girls to Qingfapu Brothels Under the Pretense of Filming Movies 191

▲ Fu Xiuqing Fortunately Redeemed by a Patron

▲ Huang Dianru Sentenced to Three Years of Imprisonment

Seventeen-year-old Xiuqing, daughter of Yong woman Fu Xu, residing at No. 38 Zhaofeng Road, was tricked by Chen Xiaofang, a Zhenjiang man who had been arrested, and his mistress Ni A'yu, into going to Qingjiangpu under the pretense of filming a movie in August of last year. She was sold to a brothel as a prostitute. Later, she was redeemed by a patron, Yang Minggao, who sent Xiuqing back to Shanghai. The two defendants confessed that a man named Wang also went to sell the girl. The detective Shen Binkui, who was handling the case, found out that the suspect's name was Huang Dianru (nickname Huang Deye), 38 years old, and he was hiding at No. 196 Chongqing Road. He reported to the former head detective and, with the cooperation of a Western detective, secretly went to the address and arrested Huang, taking him to the Huishan Police Station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police attorney Zhang Tianyin stated the previous events, saying that the defendant had been identified by the victim Fu Xiuqing and the accomplices Chen Xiaofang and Ni A'yu as the Wang who went to the Qingjiangpu brothel to sell Fu. They were all present in court today. According to Fu Xiuqing, Ni A'yu tricked me out, and the next day Chen Xiaofang, Ni A'yu, and the defendant went to Zhenjiang, staying in a certain hotel for three nights. They asked me to go to Qingjiangpu to film a movie. I knew something was wrong and didn't want to go, but the defendant beat me. I had to go and was sold to a brothel, forced to become a prostitute. The madam's name was Tianxi, and I lived a life of prostitution for two months until a patron named Yang redeemed me and sent me to Shanghai. I heard that the Yang family runs a bowl shop in Qingjiangpu and is not currently in Shanghai. According to the Yong woman Ni A'yu, who had been arrested, the defendant, nicknamed Huang Deye, was a friend of Chen Xiaofang, my lover. He indeed introduced Fu Xiuqing to the brothel in Qingjiangpu and even wanted to sell me to the brothel as well, but Chen Xiaofang did not agree. According to Chen Xiaofang, the defendant went to Qingjiangpu with me, where his friend Cai Xiaodazi brokered the sale of Fu as a prostitute. When questioned, the defendant's statement was evasive. After Judge Shen Bingrong verified the confession, he sentenced Huang Dianru to three years of imprisonment as a warning.

Organization of the Zhenzhen Society 195

Female scholars Zheng Zhenduo, Chen Naiqian, and others, aware that ancient Chinese books have repeatedly suffered destruction and that rare editions are only occasionally circulated but are too expensive to collect, and that publishers are only interested in profit and will not print books unless they are sure of sales, have organized the Zhenzhen Society, dedicated to selecting and printing rare editions from the past three hundred years that have never been reprinted. They do not limit themselves to any category and will initially print only one hundred copies of each type. The first products are facsimiles of three Ming Dynasty engraved illustrated romances (the first is Tu Long's "Xiuwen Ji," the second is Fan Shiyan's "Mingzhong Ji," and the third is Shen Ciyin's "Chuanxiao Ji"). The illustrations are meticulous, and the engraving and printing are exquisite, making them the best among Ming Dynasty books. The themes are all original in the world of romance, and together they form a perfect combination. The end includes new postscripts by Zheng and Chen, which provide detailed textual research on the books and authors, further increasing the reader's interest. Each set is finely bound in six volumes, with a cloth case, and because only one hundred copies are printed, the cost is 10 yuan. The distribution address is Zhenzhen Society, No. 55 Boulevard de Boileau.

Free Talk

Aphorisms of Ninety-Three-Year-Old Ma Xiangbo

One Can Become a Gentleman Simply by Wearing a Parisian Hat 207

— ·Jing· Record

Elder Xiang advocates for national standardized clothing, short for men and long for women, using improved fabrics of silk and hemp as raw materials. The following are the reasons he gives:

"Wearing clothes is an indispensable thing in life: it's a pity we don't pay enough attention to it. With a little adjustment, we can obtain a universally accepted uniform in society.

Because the quality of clothing is not a matter of material but rather a matter of fashion. Once it becomes a common style of dress, no one discusses its quality anymore. Do you think so?"

I agreed and continued, "When I was at Beijing Normal University, I wore a light green student uniform, the style and material of which were very bad, even worse than what the postmen wore; but everyone was happy to wear it because outsiders could tell at a glance that they were from the highest education institution!"

Elder Xiang nodded, smiled, and continued,

"Therefore, my proposal for standardized clothing is even more valid! It is best to be nationally standardized, short for men and long for women. Our country produces a lot of silk and hemp, let experts study and make clothing materials; in this way, national clothing can also promote domestic goods, wouldn't that be killing two birds with one stone?"

A few days later, a guest came and talked about this issue. In addition to restating his views and reasons, Elder Xiang also told a little anecdote:

"Italians mostly wear silk goods because they can also produce a lot of silk. But foreigners who pay attention to fashion want to imitate the French. Once, someone came to visit me, took off his hat, and said it was a Parisian hat, proving that he was a gentleman! How can one become a gentleman simply by wearing a Parisian hat? Everyone, guess!"

Modern Mulan 208

— ·Yun·Sun

|Snippets from the Shanghai Battle|

The beautiful tale of Hua Mulan joining the army, I believe, is a timeless legend. Wu Mulan is the most ardent advocate of the women's movement! Although her actions are comparable to Hua Mulan, the troops she leads are still women. She is merely the leader of an all-female army. As for Miss Mulan, the daughter of Hu Hanmin, and the many others who use "Mulan" as their elegant name, they only admire "Mulan" as a person, at most playing a game of cross-dressing.

During the January 28th Shanghai Incident, the Shanghai Boy Scouts Council, adhering to the spirit of the Boy Scouts, organized a battlefield service team, venturing deep into the line of fire to make a living. Soon, due to the vastness of the battlefield, the comrades were insufficient, so they temporarily trained a group of strong young men. Among them was Comrade Wang Kangfu, a new recruit. Initially, he was assigned to a shelter, and later to the dispatch section of the transportation department. Comrade Kangfu's work was truly astonishing! He traveled between Jiading, Nanxiang, Shanghai, and Liuhe faster than the other comrades. He had no special talents. He drove a recovery vehicle like lightning. When everyone rode horses and whipped them, he followed closely. When everyone slept together, he did not hesitate. Sometimes, when the comrades were tired and their bodies were dirty, they invited him to the bathhouse in town for a bath, and he agreed generously, but when it came to actually taking a bath, he declined.

Half a year later, we only recently discovered that Comrade Wang Kangfu, with whom we spent three months together, was a woman in disguise. A colleague of his told me that, according to his recollection, Wang Kangfu showed no signs of being female. Most noticeably, her breasts were like a man's, and her demeanor was purely masculine. She now has a lover and is about to announce her intention to live together. She is only twenty-one years old, and her origin is probably in the Jiahu area. Regarding this secret act of hers, we can only say: "In ancient times, there was Hua Mulan; today, there is Wang Kangfu."

Trendy Words 210

— ·Xi

In every era, there are new trends, and in every era, there are trendy words. In China, during the late Qing Dynasty, speaking about foreign affairs was the trendiest thing to do in official circles, from discussing diplomacy and handling military uniforms to training troops and manufacturing weapons. The phrase "Chinese learning as the foundation, Western learning for application" became a common saying. Gradually, it changed to talking about constitutionalism and implementing new policies, from opening parliament and establishing schools to mining, developing industries, and building railways. The phrase "reform and innovation" was the unanimous slogan of the nation at the time. After the Republic of China, from revolution and republic to the Northern Expedition and unification, there were no particularly trendy words commonly used in official circles during the Northern Government era! It's not that there weren't any, such as the warlords' phrases "If others do not offend me, I will not offend others" and "demanding salaries" and "disaster officials," but these are not what I want to record. After the capital moved south, many new words that are newly popular in official circles have very special colors and must be recorded. For example: (1) Looking for a job is called seeking "work." The old phrase "Where are you congratulating yourself?" is now changed to "Where are you working?" (2) Losing a job, the new name is called "unemployment." (3) Supporting a superior is called "supporting." (4) Attacking a certain faction is called "overthrowing." (5) Promoting a certain matter is called "conducting." For example, when you see someone seeking a good position, you cannot say, "How is your lobbying going?" You must change it to "How is your conducting going?" (6) Asking someone to promote you is called "introducing" or "clearing the path." (7) Promoting a certain faction or praising someone is called "propagandizing." (8) Scolding someone's lackeys is called "tools." (9) Campaigning for election is called "running for election." (10) Presenting matters is called "reporting." Just writing roughly, there are already ten types. In addition, this new bureaucratic dictionary is inexhaustible and will be continued when I am in the mood another day.

Steamed Buns and Rouge 211

— ·莲

|She Was Still Perplexed|

One day, at lunchtime after school, several companions taking the same streetcar were waiting for each other, waiting for everyone to leave together. Just as they reached the intersection of ×× Road, a streetcar flew past them.

"We missed it by a few steps, and now we have to wait another fifteen minutes. How annoying," A complained.

"I might as well go exchange two dimes for copper coins," B said, noticing that she didn't have any coins in her pocket.

"What should we do? I'm hungry," C said, pressing her hands against her stomach.

"Then let's go to that shop and eat steamed buns! We still have more than ten minutes to wait for the streetcar, so we'll have time!" B pointed to a steamed bun shop by the roadside, seeking the consent of A and C. Finally, the three of them, like hungry ghosts, walked into this rarely visited steamed bun shop. Two baskets of small steamed buns were served, and everyone grabbed them and started eating without thinking. After taking a bite, C discovered a red, blood-like color on the steamed bun and was so frightened that she dared not swallow it. A and B also paid attention to their own steamed buns, but there was nothing on theirs. C was even more angry, her almond eyes wide open, and she took the steamed bun to the shopkeeper to argue: "Look, how can you sell such dirty things?" The shopkeepers, caught off guard, didn't have any appropriate words to answer!

Just then, A and B were as happy as Columbus discovering the New World because they realized that C's red and greasy lips were the reason why the steamed bun was red. They winked at C, and a flush of red spread across C's cheeks. Thus, they left that steamed bun shop. |It's true: "There's nothing really wrong, but fools worry themselves."

Postal Partners Entering the Pass (11) 212

— ·Seeking·Happiness·Studio·Owner

The phrase "lifelong happiness" seemed like a sharp arrow piercing Lu Boqin's heart. He suddenly felt a chill down his spine, shaking him awake from his dazed state. His mind immediately cleared, and he remembered the idea he had decided on last night, which was extremely correct and should not be shaken or changed by his current confusion. He quickly mustered his courage, put in some self-control, and poured out the sentences he had carefully prepared:

"I'm sorry, I'm afraid my answer today won't satisfy you."

Tong Yizhen's expression changed abruptly. He also hurriedly lowered his eyelids and said in one breath, "I have considered it very carefully. I really cannot agree with the kind of liberation you proposed. Because running away rashly together will definitely lead to unfortunate results in the future and leave endless regrets. Think about it! We are both very young and don't have much ability. Besides doing a small job at the post office here, I'm afraid I won't be able to find a comparable job elsewhere. The problem of our family life after we run away will trap us in a stalemate. I appreciate your heartfelt love, and I'm willing to sacrifice anything. But we should put your happiness first. That way won't make you happy in the future, and it will cause you endless pain and damage in spirit, body, and reputation. How can I risk doing it without considering it? Yizhen, I love you, so I can't hurt you. You should understand my good intentions."

Tong Yizhen couldn't bear to listen any longer. Tears welled up and covered her face, which was filled with disappointment, grief, and misery. Unexpectedly, she grabbed the umbrella, stood up, and left. Only with her back turned did she say such piercing words:

"I don't want to hear you talk. What do you mean by thinking about my happiness? Yet you're willing to let me be someone else's fifth concubine? Is that my great happiness? I understand. You don't have the revolutionary spirit of modern young people, you're afraid to take risks for love, and you can't bear to sacrifice that little rice bowl at the post office, so you can bear to ignore my affairs. You're too cowardly!"

Lu Boqin was so frightened that he hurriedly chased after her. She turned around and spat, saying, "It's not just cowardly, I'm going to call you despicable. I, Tong Yizhen, have been blind, recognizing the wrong person, and foolishly wanting to take you, a despicable thing, as a lover to rely on. Now I see you clearly. There's no need to talk anymore. From now on, no one cares about anyone, no one knows anyone anymore. Let's do our own things."

Remarks

Saving the Nation Through the Buddhist Altar 213

— ·佛

The Panchen Lama has already arrived in Beiping and will soon open the "Kalachakra Dharma Assembly to Pacify Disasters" in Beiping. That's great. Human power cannot save the nation, so we can only ask the bodhisattvas to save the nation.

Any politician, any military strategist, or any ideological system, once it comes to China, is always helpless. If it's not done well, "madness, tuberculosis, bloating, and obstruction," all four are incurable diseases. China's illness originally combines all four, so no matter how famous a doctor is invited to diagnose and prescribe medicine, it's mostly ineffective and can only await death. We must invite great immortals like Hua Tuo and Lu Chunyang to diagnose and treat it.

China is originally a country of many gods. Establishing teachings through divine ways is originally the first fundamental law of governing the country. Books like "The Investiture of the Gods" and "Journey to the West" are originally national treasures of our country. Jiang Ziya, Liu Bowen, Wang Chanlao, Bai Niangniang, Hongxian, and Nie Yinniang are originally representative figures in our country's history. Now that our country is plagued by internal and external troubles and is in a state of disarray, as long as one great immortal accidentally violates heavenly laws and is demoted to the mortal world, or their worldly karma is not yet exhausted and they fall into the mortal realm, then our country's savior will arrive.

The Buddha Dharma is boundless and its supernatural powers are vast. Sun Wukong somersaulted dozens of times, but he still couldn't escape the Buddha's five fingers. Since ancient times, the Xiongnu, Turks, Jurchens, Khitans, and various barbarians, no matter how fierce they were, once they came to China, they were completely assimilated. This is also a sign of the boundless Buddha Dharma. Although Japan is tyrannical and acts recklessly, it will definitely not escape the Tathagata's yin-yang calculations.

Since the September 18th Incident, our country's authorities have wholeheartedly prayed day and night to the League of Nations Bodhisattva to save them from suffering and disaster. Now, the report equivalent to a divine oracle has already been issued. Although the League of Nations has not yet held a meeting to discuss it, and the outcome is still unclear, judging from this divine oracle, our country's illness has no hope of recovery. It can be seen that the League of Nations is ultimately human and not divine, and the Old Man of Heaven is not effective.

Now that the Kalachakra Dharma Assembly is being held, all the great bodhisattvas will surely descend, opening great wisdom and turning the great Dharma wheel, and will surely subdue all the goblins, demons, and monsters under the altar one by one. Since there is a disaster-pacifying altar with boundless Buddha Dharma and vast supernatural powers, there must be unexpected effectiveness. We should wait and see.

Science

Method of Making Plaster Statues 215

— ·枕

The method of making plaster statues uses the property of calcined gypsum to absorb water and combine. Ordinary crystalline gypsum contains two molecules of water of crystallization (CaSO5·2H2O). When calcined for a certain time, it loses one molecule of water of crystallization and becomes calcined gypsum (CaSO4H2O). After mixing with water, it dries into a white solid block in about fifteen minutes, which can be carved. Before making a plaster statue, a mold must be made first.

(1) Making the Mold. To make the mold, the original object (such as a doll if you want to make a mold of a doll) must first be coated with a semi-solid oil, such as petroleum jelly or thick soapy water. Knead clay into long strips, the height of which is equal to the thickness of the mold to be made. Then surround the clay strips around the side edge of the original object. Then mix gypsum with water to form a thick paste and fill in any side surrounded by the clay strips. After the gypsum is dry, remove the clay strips, and the gypsum will adhere to the original object. Pry it off by hand. At a certain distance from the edge of the gypsum, dig a small square notch. Coat the edge and the inside of the notch with oil. Fit it in the original place and mix gypsum again to fill the other side. The second piece of the mold is made with a protruding part that matches the small notch of the previous piece of the mold. After doing this, you can cast a plaster statue or a wax statue. The above is the simplest method for making a mold for casting a plaster statue. If the object has uneven concavity and convexity and is full of curves, it is not applicable. Therefore, the mold for making a plaster statue can have up to ten or more pieces. When making the statue, the molds must be joined together, tied tightly with ropes, and gypsum is poured in through a hole of appropriate size at the bottom of the mold. Ordinary molds for casting wax statues are only made of two pieces, and there is no need for a larger hole, only a hole that can accommodate a goose feather tube is enough.

(2) Making the Plaster Statue. Mix calcined gypsum into a thin paste and pour it in from the bottom of the mold. The amount depends on the size of the mold. After pouring, rotate the mold so that the inside of the mold is evenly covered with gypsum. It can solidify in two or three minutes. Then remove the mold. At this time, the plaster statue is complete, but there will be protruding lines at the joints of the mold, which can be removed with a knife. Then rub it with horsetail grass or fine sandpaper to complete it.

Over time, the plaster statue often becomes dull and unsightly. Never wipe it with wet objects. First wipe it with a dry cloth, and then rub it with horsetail grass to make it as white as new.

(3) Making the Wax Statue. Heat and melt the wax, dye it with various colors, and pour it into the lower part of the mold. Then cover the upper part of the mold, shake it quickly, insert a goose feather tube about an inch long into the small hole of the mold, blow it hard, and quickly put it into cold water. Separate the mold, and the wax statue will float to the surface of the water. Remove the seam lines of the mold, and correct the goose feather tube hole to complete a perfect wax statue.

Improvement of Society Discussion Society

Deliberations on the School Fee Issue 216

— ·

Social construction is based on money, and education will eventually become commercialized! This kind of social pathology can only be blamed on the bad results that our government should have. If the government's method of running education does not violate the principles of socialism, then a portion of the taxes paid by the people is enough to provide beautiful educational institutions and educational administration. People of the appropriate age have the right to receive education, and the government is always responsible for "teaching" and "raising." Then, the problem of paying fees will naturally disappear, only because the government runs education only with nominal but not real intentions, inappropriately distributes the taxes of the poor and common people, resulting in professors demanding salaries, students going on strike, principals embezzling public funds, and political tides manipulating students, and many other malpractices are countless. National education cannot satisfy the people, so the establishment of private educational institutions follows, and then the problem of paying fees arises and the situation of entanglement is discovered.

Committing private fraud is due to the long-term historical changes of China and the relationship of vast areas, and the bad national character that has become deeply ingrained by the people's accumulated habits and following the old ways. The money earned by the people's blood and sweat passes through the hands of politicians, and big money turns into small money, and small money turns into no money. As a result, those who run education become even more aggravated and openly operate a business. How can this kind of atmosphere allow the poor to rise above, and how can China become rich and strong? The discussion in this article does not focus on the issue of whether or not various fees should be paid or the amount of payment, because those who use public office for private gain will never defraud "without a legitimate reason." What we pay attention to is the use of the fees after they are paid. What we want to prevent is private fraud after the fees are paid. Now, let's say the most important methods for everyone to comment on.

(1) Open School Finances. School finances must not only be cleared by accountants, but also an organized mixed supervisory committee must be formed. The candidates will be represented by the Social Affairs Bureau, student parents, school directors, and famous people from the society. The powers of the supervisory committee are to review the budget, audit finances, and report those who commit private fraud. Then, the school's finances have been supervised by the whole society, and the habit of indiscriminate spending can be eliminated.

(2) The use of money from school income should be based on the principle of consumer cooperation, and it must never be profited from. If the economy is not sufficient, why not reduce the scope, strive for practicality, and not be greedy for false fame. For example, meal expenses, book sales, accommodation expenses, libraries, experiment expenses, and sports expenses should have student representatives participating in cooperation and monitoring at the same time. Their obligation is to publicize the situation at any time. Students above high school should select representatives, while in primary and secondary schools, the school authorities will report to the school supervisory committee every month and the school supervisory committee will send staff to investigate openly and secretly at any time.

(3) The standard of fees for major primary and secondary schools should first be researched and stipulated by education experts, with the aim of popularizing education. Later, each school can slightly change it according to the location. National schools have monthly government subsidies,

Page 19

Therefore, the burden on students is naturally reduced, and the burden on private schools is relatively heavier, but it is fortunate that the money spent does not go into the private pockets of a few people. As for enjoying the government's right to "teach" and "raise," our common people can only pray and hope.

In short, education expenses have a civilian standard, the principle of usage is based on consumer cooperation, and when expenses are used, they are supervised by the whole society, and the problem of paying fees will naturally be solved, and profit-making educational institutions will also be eliminated. There is no need for us to be verbose.

Organization of Society

Whose Fault Is It?

— ·洪·水

Once, when I was sick, I lay for a whole night and half a day in a pavilion where no sunlight came in. The heavy air was really unbearable. The eldest son of the second landlord was enthusiastically humming Peking opera tunes in the hall. At that time, my head almost hurt so badly that it was about to burst open, so I had to go out on the street for a walk. I happened to wander into a construction site where houses were being built. Everything seemed ordinary, except for a short, lively young worker, estimated to be only thirteen or fourteen years old, but with two heavy buckets of mud on his slanted and narrow shoulders, which attracted my great attention! "Child, how's the work going?" I asked him kindly with a smile.

"! Not bad, sir!"

"What's your name? You're probably thirteen or fourteen years old, right?"

"No, I'm already sixteen years old. Sir, my name is A'gen, and my surname is Wang."

"Ah! A'gen, you look very young, you don't look like you're sixteen or seventeen years old."

"I can't be compared to ordinary people, because most people's living environment is beautiful and pleasant, they eat well, wear well, and their bodies naturally develop faster. Like me, I was born with a hard life. Since I was young, I couldn't talk about nutrition and protection, and I also had to do hard labor. Naturally, my development couldn't be healthy, and I grew up with such a short stature. It's really 'Eating a lot doesn't make me big.' Haha! Sir, please don't laugh at me. I'm a child who doesn't lie!" At the same time, he put down the two buckets of mud he was carrying and held the carrying pole straight, as if waiting for me to respond.

"What do your parents do?"

"Alas! My dad was also a mason. Unfortunately, he accidentally fell from the fifth floor while building a house for Master Shen two years ago, and his brains splattered everywhere, and he died instantly. My mom does mending work for a living. There, she's mending clothes for the workers over there!" A'gen pointed to a woman sitting on a small stool under the shade of a tree across the street, tirelessly wielding a needle. The woman was holding a baby with a big head and a thin neck, who was crying softly, sucking on her nipple. A'gen then said softly, "The baby my mom is holding is my little brother. He's a posthumous child. He's also often sick and cries a lot. How would he know that he lost his father before he was even born, a poor orphan!"

"Oh! That's so pitiful! How was your father's funeral handled?"

"Sir, speaking of this, it must be said that my dad was a good person when he was alive, so his workers, who are also my foremen, tried their best to ask Master Shen for help. They finally got 150 old silver dollars to settle the matter. My foreman also took pity on our widow and orphans, and treated me as a senior worker. Although the work is a bit too much for me to handle, I grit my teeth and try hard to struggle, and I don't feel much of anything."

"How much do you get paid a day?"

"Four dimes, the meals are paid for by the company, and the side dishes are paid for by myself. This is considered a senior worker!"

"Wow! So senior workers only get four dimes."

"Sir, look, the junior workers who are hammering stones and sifting soil all day long, or carrying heavy objects, shout 'Hang Yu' 'Hang Yu' all night long, and each person only gets two dimes." He pointed to a group of people who were doing heavy work, shouting back and forth. At the same time, a kind of smile of "more than enough compared to those below" and "sufficient to comfort myself" seemed to float on his face. "Labor is sacred, that's not wrong. A'gen, I envy you very much. At such a young age, you can support yourself. I also want to come and work. Can you find a senior worker position for me?"

"Haha! How can you compare to us poor people? We should be the ones building houses. Building this one and building that one, but we suffer until we're old and still don't have a house to live in. Sir, instead of taking pity on us, you still want to make fun of us?"

A'gen carried the buckets of mud and flew up the steps to the roof. Although I couldn't continue talking to him, it raised a question: those who build houses are one group of people, and those who live in houses are another group of people. What the child said makes some sense, but what is the fault for society creating such unfair things?

School Photographs

Request for Early Departure Due to Important Matters 217

— ·Shen· Xiu

On Tuesday afternoon, during the third period, while the class was studying official document formats, less than thirty minutes in, several students suddenly began to snicker. Oh? It turned out that a female student sitting near the classroom door had packed up her books and left without saying goodbye to the teacher.

Leaving during class time without informing the teacher is usually a common occurrence, but with female students, it cannot be viewed the same as male students. It seems worthy of our attention. In less than a minute, another female student left in the same manner. What was the reason for this? Many male students naturally did not understand and snickered even more loudly than the first. The snickering had not yet stopped when a third female student left through the doorway. At that point, the male students' mood gradually became agitated, and they snickered in unison, scaring the female student into practically running away.

Three female students left in a row. The teacher, because of his special consideration for female students, did not pursue the matter. Especially our official document format teacher, who was so amiable, didn't interfere with them. Therefore, the male students' snickering was naturally not prohibited either.

There were still two female students sitting further inside, who, when leaving, would naturally have to pass in front of the teacher. Passing in front of the teacher without informing him made them feel a little embarrassed, and the male students' snickering added to the difficulty. Asking was difficult for the female students who were prone to shyness, truly a dilemma. However, watching the three female students leave, already three or four minutes had passed. These two female students seemed to show signs of anxiety. They had no choice but to write a note, which they passed to the teacher. The teacher took it and nodded slightly. The two female students then left, looking both shy and pleased, with their heads bowed. Oh! The slight nod, it turned out, indicated permission for them to leave. As they left, the male students, as before, sent a few snickers!

Now that the female students had completely left, many male students rushed to see the note that the female students had passed to the official document format teacher, craning their necks, asking each other, causing a disruption. The teacher, catering to the majority of the students' wishes, dismissed the class.

Look! Look! A burst of shouts. What did the female students write? Very simply, it was written, "Request for early departure due to important matters," six characters. These six characters became the topic of conversation and speculation for the male students that evening.

A Corner of Society

Exchanging Small Change 218

— ·Kang· Shi

The other day, I passed by the North Railway Station and saw a shop assistant at a cigarette and paper shop arguing with a man in a Western suit about exchanging small change. I felt that this matter was detrimental to the character of merchants and also an undesirable state of society. Therefore, I am writing it down below.

"Many shops exchange two dimes for five hundred cash, why do you only exchange it for four hundred and eighty cash here?" the man in the Western suit questioned the shop assistant.

"This is the railway station, it cannot be compared to other places!" the shop assistant replied with a stern face.

"Then why don't you put up a sign? Clearly stating that two dimes are exchanged for four hundred and eighty cash!" the man in the Western suit continued to question.

"Just be easygoing, give him one more copper coin!" another shop assistant said.

"No way! Isn't there a cigarette and paper shop across the street that is hanging a sign saying that two dimes are exchanged for five hundred cash?" the man in the Western suit retorted, pointing to a cigarette and paper shop across the street.

"Just give him back the small change!" another shop assistant said again.

The man in the Western suit saw how arrogant the shop assistant was! Naturally, his anger flared up, and he cursed loudly, "Scoundrel! Come out here!"

Fortunately, others came to mediate, and a storm was averted. After the man in the Western suit left, the shop assistant grumbled, "Miser! Dressed in a nice Western suit, trying to haggle over one or two copper coins to death, really a miser..."

Almost everyone in Shanghai has encountered the above situation. Alas! Not at all different from "merchants love wealth" and "lost integrity". However, nowadays everyone, especially important people, has the despicable traits of merchants, relying solely on deceptive tactics to make a living!

Finally, I want to tell everyone, never exchange foreign currency or small change at places like tram stations and railway stations, because the general cigarette and paper shops here all employ greedy tactics of hoarding!

The litigation costs are borne by the defendants. ▲ Xu Xishan vs. Chen Xitang over payment for loan (Main text): The defendant should repay the plaintiff 200 silver dollars and pay interest at 1.6% per month from January 6, 1931, until the date of execution. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant. ▲ Xie Pingfeng vs. Pan Hegao over rent payment and return of premises (Main text): The defendant should pay the plaintiff 320 silver dollars in rent. The plaintiff's remaining requests are dismissed. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant five-sixths and the plaintiff one-sixth. ▲ Liu Zhengfang vs. Tang Shida et al. over bill payment (Main text): The defendant Tang Shida should pay the plaintiff 530 silver dollars. If execution is ineffective, the defendant Yang Xiangsheng should repay on his behalf. The litigation costs are borne by the defendants.

Shanghai Local Court 221

▲ Civil Judgment: In the case of Wu Jichang vs. Ruan Guangshan regarding rent arrears and eviction, the defendant should pay the plaintiff rent of $213.40 and vacate the city house at No. 182 Lan Ni Du Avenue. The expenses shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ In the case of Tang Shu Yong vs. Tianyi Machinery Factory over rice money, the defendant should pay the plaintiff rice money of $58.90, and the litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ In the mutual lawsuit between Jin Yuqi and Pan Shoukai, etc., regarding advance payments and compensation, the defendant Pan Shoukai should repay the plaintiff $154.784. The plaintiff's lawsuit against the defendant Zhu Yiyi and others is dismissed. The counterclaim defendant should pay the counterclaim plaintiff damages of $360. The remaining counterclaim of the counterclaim plaintiff is dismissed. The plaintiff shall bear 7/10 of the litigation fee for the original lawsuit, and the defendant Pan Shoukai shall bear 3/10. The litigation fee for the counterclaim shall be borne equally by both parties. ▲ In the case of Meng Yuemin vs. Chen Laifa over rice money, the defendant should pay the plaintiff $84. This amount should be repaid in installments of $20 per month until cleared. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. ▲ vs. Dai Afa, in the case of a dispute over profit sharing, the plaintiff's lawsuit is dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiff.

▲ Civil Ruling: In the case of Peng Daxing, etc. vs. Wu Desen regarding funeral expenses, a request to transfer the case file to the First Special District Court for trial. Having reviewed the petition, it is found that the case file has already been transferred to the Shanghai First Special District Court for trial by this court on June 8 of this year. This notification is hereby issued. ▲ Xu Maoquan applies for record filing because Tian Dan's wife was taken away. Having reviewed the petition, it is stated that Tian Dan's wife was taken away, fearing theft, sale, or mortgage. Since a public notice has been issued declaring the original certificate invalid and requesting a new one, there is no need to apply for record filing again. This notification is hereby issued.

▲ Criminal Judgment: Peng Fentai is sentenced to three months imprisonment for causing death due to negligence in business. The number of days in pre-trial detention shall be deducted from the term of imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. Peng Fentai should pay the funeral expenses and compensation of Jin Maomao, totaling $400. ▲ Xie Fu is sentenced to six months imprisonment for attempting to rape and entice a woman under the age of twenty. ▲ Ruling: The private prosecution in the Feng Quqing embezzlement case is dismissed. ▲ Chen Sanlang is sentenced to six months imprisonment for theft at the wharf. ▲ Shi Ajin, Sun Xiaobao, and Jin Lishan are each sentenced to six months imprisonment for joint theft. (All of the above are dated October 11th)

The appellee shall bear the litigation costs of both the first and second instances. ▲ In the appeal case of Chen Deseng vs. Liu Yueshan regarding a loan (Principal Sentence): The appeal is dismissed. The second-instance litigation costs shall be borne by the appellant. ▲ In the appeal case of Tian Shuzhou vs. Hefeng Trading Company and Gui Lin regarding bill money (Principal Sentence): The appeal is dismissed. The second-instance litigation costs shall be borne by the appellant. ▲ In the appeal case of Li Sipei, etc. vs. Gu Rongchi regarding damages (Principal Sentence): The original judgment is altered regarding the amount of compensation and litigation costs. The appellants, etc. shall jointly bear the litigation costs of the first and second instances. ▲ In the appeal case of Hetae Company vs. Shen Biecun regarding the delivery of rent arrears and eviction (Principal Sentence): The original judgment is altered except for the part ordering the appellee to reimburse the appellant $680.
